Type A^{1}_9.The letter \(h\) stands for elements of the Cartan subalgebra,
the letter \(g\) stands for the Chevalley (root space) generators of non-zero weight.
The generator \(h_i\) is the element of the Cartan subalgebra dual to the
i^th simple root, that is, \([h_i, g] =\langle \alpha_i , \gamma\rangle g\),
where g is a Chevalley generator, \(\gamma\) is its weight, and
\(\alpha_i\) is the i^th simple root.
The Lie bracket table is too large to be rendered in LaTeX, displaying in html format instead.

We define the symmetric Cartan matrix
by requesting that the entry in the i-th row and j-th column
be the scalar product of the i^th and j^th roots. The symmetric Cartan matrix is:
\(\begin{pmatrix}2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2\\ \end{pmatrix}\)
Let the (i, j)^{th} entry of the symmetric Cartan matrix be a_{ij}.
Then we define the co-symmetric Cartan matrix as the matrix whose (i, j)^{th} entry equals 4*a_{ij}/(a_{ii}*a_{jj}). In other words, the co-symmetric Cartan matrix is the symmetric Cartan matrix of the dual root system. The co-symmetric Cartan matrix equals:
\(\begin{pmatrix}2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1 & 0\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2 & -1\\ 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & -1 & 2\\ \end{pmatrix}\)
The determinant of the symmetric Cartan matrix is: 10
Half sum of positive roots: (9/2, 8, 21/2, 12, 25/2, 12, 21/2, 8, 9/2)= \(9/2\varepsilon_{1}+7/2\varepsilon_{2}+5/2\varepsilon_{3}+3/2\varepsilon_{4}+1/2\varepsilon_{5}-1/2\varepsilon_{6}-3/2\varepsilon_{7}-5/2\varepsilon_{8}-7/2\varepsilon_{9}-9/2\varepsilon_{10}\)
The fundamental weights (the j^th fundamental weight has scalar product 1
with the j^th simple root times 2 divided by the root length squared,
and 0 with the remaining simple roots):
(9/10, 4/5, 7/10, 3/5, 1/2, 2/5, 3/10, 1/5, 1/10) = \(9/10\varepsilon_{1}-1/10\varepsilon_{2}-1/10\varepsilon_{3}-1/10\varepsilon_{4}-1/10\varepsilon_{5}-1/10\varepsilon_{6}-1/10\varepsilon_{7}-1/10\varepsilon_{8}-1/10\varepsilon_{9}-1/10\varepsilon_{10}\)
(4/5, 8/5, 7/5, 6/5, 1, 4/5, 3/5, 2/5, 1/5) = \(4/5\varepsilon_{1}+4/5\varepsilon_{2}-1/5\varepsilon_{3}-1/5\varepsilon_{4}-1/5\varepsilon_{5}-1/5\varepsilon_{6}-1/5\varepsilon_{7}-1/5\varepsilon_{8}-1/5\varepsilon_{9}-1/5\varepsilon_{10}\)
(7/10, 7/5, 21/10, 9/5, 3/2, 6/5, 9/10, 3/5, 3/10) = \(7/10\varepsilon_{1}+7/10\varepsilon_{2}+7/10\varepsilon_{3}-3/10\varepsilon_{4}-3/10\varepsilon_{5}-3/10\varepsilon_{6}-3/10\varepsilon_{7}-3/10\varepsilon_{8}-3/10\varepsilon_{9}-3/10\varepsilon_{10}\)
(3/5, 6/5, 9/5, 12/5, 2, 8/5, 6/5, 4/5, 2/5) = \(3/5\varepsilon_{1}+3/5\varepsilon_{2}+3/5\varepsilon_{3}+3/5\varepsilon_{4}-2/5\varepsilon_{5}-2/5\varepsilon_{6}-2/5\varepsilon_{7}-2/5\varepsilon_{8}-2/5\varepsilon_{9}-2/5\varepsilon_{10}\)
(1/2, 1, 3/2, 2, 5/2, 2, 3/2, 1, 1/2) = \(1/2\varepsilon_{1}+1/2\varepsilon_{2}+1/2\varepsilon_{3}+1/2\varepsilon_{4}+1/2\varepsilon_{5}-1/2\varepsilon_{6}-1/2\varepsilon_{7}-1/2\varepsilon_{8}-1/2\varepsilon_{9}-1/2\varepsilon_{10}\)
(2/5, 4/5, 6/5, 8/5, 2, 12/5, 9/5, 6/5, 3/5) = \(2/5\varepsilon_{1}+2/5\varepsilon_{2}+2/5\varepsilon_{3}+2/5\varepsilon_{4}+2/5\varepsilon_{5}+2/5\varepsilon_{6}-3/5\varepsilon_{7}-3/5\varepsilon_{8}-3/5\varepsilon_{9}-3/5\varepsilon_{10}\)
(3/10, 3/5, 9/10, 6/5, 3/2, 9/5, 21/10, 7/5, 7/10) = \(3/10\varepsilon_{1}+3/10\varepsilon_{2}+3/10\varepsilon_{3}+3/10\varepsilon_{4}+3/10\varepsilon_{5}+3/10\varepsilon_{6}+3/10\varepsilon_{7}-7/10\varepsilon_{8}-7/10\varepsilon_{9}-7/10\varepsilon_{10}\)
(1/5, 2/5, 3/5, 4/5, 1, 6/5, 7/5, 8/5, 4/5) = \(1/5\varepsilon_{1}+1/5\varepsilon_{2}+1/5\varepsilon_{3}+1/5\varepsilon_{4}+1/5\varepsilon_{5}+1/5\varepsilon_{6}+1/5\varepsilon_{7}+1/5\varepsilon_{8}-4/5\varepsilon_{9}-4/5\varepsilon_{10}\)
(1/10, 1/5, 3/10, 2/5, 1/2, 3/5, 7/10, 4/5, 9/10) = \(1/10\varepsilon_{1}+1/10\varepsilon_{2}+1/10\varepsilon_{3}+1/10\varepsilon_{4}+1/10\varepsilon_{5}+1/10\varepsilon_{6}+1/10\varepsilon_{7}+1/10\varepsilon_{8}+1/10\varepsilon_{9}-9/10\varepsilon_{10}\)
Below is the simple basis realized in epsilon coordinates. Please note that the epsilon coordinate realizations do not have long roots of length of 2 in types G and C. This means that gramm matrix (w.r.t. the standard scalar product) of the epsilon coordinate realizations in types G and C does not equal the corresponding symmetric Cartan matrix.
(1, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0) = \(\varepsilon_{1}-\varepsilon_{2}\)

(0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 1) = \(\varepsilon_{9}-\varepsilon_{10}\)
